## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The rate of change of concentration (dA_dt) is the reaction rate, which in chemical kinetics is typically expressed as a function of the reactant concentration (A). While simple rate laws depend only on A, explicit time (t) dependence can arise from non-isothermal conditions, catalyst deactivation, or fractal kinetics, making dA_dt a function of both A and t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of A and t)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (exponential decay of A)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular decay)
- nth-order power-law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general reaction order with fitted exponent)
- Michaelis-Menten saturation: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme or surface saturation kinetics)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / ((c1 + A) * (1 + c2 * A)) (rate decreases at high A)
- Autocatalytic logistic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed reaction, symmetric bell-shaped rate)
- Time-dependent rate constant (exponential): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (e.g., temperature ramp influencing rate constant)
- Time-dependent rate constant (power-law): dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A (fractal kinetics or diffusion-limited time dependence)
- Combined power-law: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A**c2 (empirical time-dependent order)
- Reversible first-order (closed system): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (linear dependence with intercept from back-reaction)
- Modified Arrhenius time dependence: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 / (c2 + t)) * A (temperature ramping with 1/T dependence)
- Prout-Tompkins autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A)**c3 (nucleation-growth with acceleratory phase)
- Sigmoidal conversion: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A)**c3 (generalized solid-state reaction rate)
- Exponential concentration dependence: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * A) (non-standard, e.g., autocatalytic explosion)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Constant reaction rate â†’ dA_dt independent of A (zero-order kinetics)
- Rate proportional to A raised to a power â†’ simple nth-order kinetics, elementary or lumped reactions
- Rate saturates at high A â†’ Michaelis-Menten or Langmuir-Hinshelwood type, indicating a rate-limiting step
- Rate increases then decreases with A â†’ autocatalytic or product-inhibited kinetics, bell-shaped rate profile
- Rate includes explicit time factor â†’ non-isothermal, catalyst aging, or fractal-like kinetics
- Linear rate with both intercept and slope in A â†’ reversible reaction under mass balance constraint
- Rate scales with time via power-law â†’ fractal or diffusion-limited kinetics in heterogeneous media
- Exponential dependence on time â†’ Arrhenius-type temperature ramping where T = T0 + خ²t
- Rate maximum at some A then falls â†’ substrate inhibition or nucleation-growth with reactant depletion
- Multiplicative time and concentration terms â†’ separable time- and concentration-dependent rate constants, often used in solid-state kinetics
